  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer3375038771969481823">Eden Newman must mate before her 18th birthday in six months or she'll be left outside to die in a burning world. But who will pick up her mate-option when she's cursed with white skin and a tragically low mate-rate of 15%? In a post-apocalyptic, totalitarian, underground world where class and beauty are defined by resistance to an overheated environment, Eden's coloring b</span>
  <span id="freeText3375038771969481823" style="display:none">Eden Newman must mate before her 18th birthday in six months or she'll be left outside to die in a burning world. But who will pick up her mate-option when she's cursed with white skin and a tragically low mate-rate of 15%? In a post-apocalyptic, totalitarian, underground world where class and beauty are defined by resistance to an overheated environment, Eden's coloring brands her as a member of the lowest class, a weak and ugly Pearl. If only she can mate with a dark-skinned Coal from the ruling class, she'll be safe. Just maybe one Coal sees the Real Eden and will be her salvation her co-worker Jamal has begun secretly dating her. But when Eden unwittingly compromises her father's secret biological experiment, she finds herself in the eye of a storm and thrown into the last area of rainforest, a strange and dangerous land. Eden must fight to save her father, who may be humanity's last hope, while standing up to a powerful beast-man she believes is her enemy, despite her overwhelming attraction. Eden must change to survive but only if she can redefine her ideas of beauty and of love, along with a little help from her "adopted aunt" Emily Dickinson.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3375038771969481823" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/1677162-is-this-a-ripoff-of-noughts-crosses">Is this a ripoff of Noughts &amp; Crosses? Because it sounds an awful lot like a ripoff of Noughts and Crosses.</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_1677162'><a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F12393909-revealing-eden">like</a></span>

<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/1677162-is-this-a-ripoff-of-noughts-crosses">one year ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/1677162-is-this-a-ripoff-of-noughts-crosses">Add your answer</a>
</li>
</ul>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/11409152-book-keeper"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1362764100i/11409152._UY100_CR30,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/11409152-book-keeper">Book Keeper</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Simply put, No. Though it depends on your definition of ripoff. Are pineapples rip-offs of apples? They are both fruit after all. <br/>Naughts & Crosses, i<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Simply put, No. Though it depends on your definition of ripoff. Are pineapples rip-offs of apples? They are both fruit after all. <br />Naughts &amp; Crosses, is a fiction book written by a British author with an alternate history back ground where crosses are the oppressors of the naughts. <br />Revealing Eden, is a sci-fi/fantasy book with a dystopian back ground were the environment has changed effecting human existence and had societal ramifications. <br />Both express aspects of racism from the darker skinned against the lighter skinned. <br />The bulk of the N&amp;Cs series was published before 2009 and a decade long hiatus before publishing again in the N&amp;C series. Saving the pearls series was published during the hiatus. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_379942274" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/379942274" />
    <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair"><img alt="Steph Sinclair" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457555690p2/4642710.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/379942274?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steph Sinclair" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair">Steph Sinclair</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">I weep for humanity </span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=serve-me-up-insta-love">serve-me-up-insta-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=strange">strange</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=bound-to-inflict-a-migraine">bound-to-inflict-a-migraine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=le-sigh">le-sigh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2012-reads">2012-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=ahhhhh-my-eyes">ahhhhh-my-eyes</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer379942274" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2006137008447580186"><blockquote>
<br/><em>"I believe that anyone who reads the novel will understand its strong stance against racism."</em><br/>-Victoria Fyot (Judging A Book By Its Cover Gives Birth To Racism)<br/>
</blockquote><br/>Well, I hate to be the bearer of bad news, but you failed. Badly. To say <em>Revealing Eden</em> is offensive is such a massive understatement. I couldn't even stomach more that a few pages at a time. It was like taking a spork to your eye, but then it breaks leaving you with only the handle to carry out your dark deed. Even with the obvious raci</span>
  <span id="freeText2006137008447580186" style="display:none"><blockquote>
<br><em>"I believe that anyone who reads the novel will understand its strong stance against racism."</em><br>-Victoria Fyot (Judging A Book By Its Cover Gives Birth To Racism)<br>
</blockquote><br>Well, I hate to be the bearer of bad news, but you failed. Badly. To say <em>Revealing Eden</em> is offensive is such a massive understatement. I couldn't even stomach more that a few pages at a time. It was like taking a spork to your eye, but then it breaks leaving you with only the handle to carry out your dark deed. Even with the obvious racism aside, the Revealing Eden is simply not good. From the dialogue to the characters to the plot, it was very badly written. A tragic mess.<br><br>There are a few things you should know before reading this review:<br><br><b>1.</b> I am an African-American.<br><b>2.</b> I went into this book knowing I would probably dislike it. Why?<br>	-Because I'm obviously masochistic.<br>	-Because I'm taking one for the team. You're welcome.<br>	-Because Foyt <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author_blog_posts/2290748-interracial-relationships-seen-through-eyes-of-young-adults" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">made a statement</a> that not many African-Americans had read her book. Here I am and yes, we still exist.<br><b>3.</b> I will most likely address a few statements made by Foyt about her novel as it pertains to <em>Revealing Eden.</em><br><b>4.</b> Oh, and this review is kinda long. Sorry about that. LOADS to cover. &gt;.&lt;<br><br>Apparently, according to Victoria Foyt the population of white people have plummeted due to an increase in sun radiation, leaving black people in charge. My first issue was with the lack of science in that premise. (And no. Throwing out random scientific names of insects, animals and plants does not signify that you've done your homework.) If the sun's radiation was *that* bad, being black won't do you that much good. What's even more odd is that for majority of the novel, Eden is hanging out outside <strong>in the sun without </strong>her coating (more on that later).<strong> </strong>I kept waiting for her to complain about how hot it was or that her skin felt burnt, but it never happened. Her father is working in a lab attempting to genetically alter people so that they have animal traits and no one has created a better sunblock or, I don't know, CURED CANCER?! Where is the logic in that?<br><br>Whites in this novel are considered a burden to society since they have such a low rate of survival. If one does not have a mate by age 18, they are to be sentenced to death. There seems to be an obvious solution to this hypothetical problem: breed out the weaker genetics. But instead white people are oppressed just for the sake of oppression. And even though Eden knows she has had two mating offers, she refuses to accept either one, choosing to wait for her "Dark Prince" in hopes that he will pick up her mating option. Her reasoning?<br><blockquote>"Because I don't want my child to be all Pearl. I'd rather be dead than mate with one of my kind."</blockquote><br>*sigh* I can't believe I have to break this down, but if a black person and a white person have a baby, that doesn't automatically guarantee a dark-skinned baby. In fact, some may have very fair complexion. Funny thing the way genetics works. But what did I expect? Almost all the dark-skinned people in <em>Revealing Eden</em> were black as night. The one person who <em>is</em> mentioned with brown skin is assumed to be mixed. *Shaking my head* It was then I should have realized that logic was not going to be <em>Revealing Eden's</em> strong point.<br><br>In order for Eden to fit in, she walks around with a coating of "Midnight Luster" on her skin and hair. She talks about dying her hair black and I couldn't figure out why she was doing that. Doesn't Foyt know that black peoples' hair is not actually black? Is that a common misconception even today? It's weird because it's something I've never thought of before. Sure, there are some whose hair is black, but it's not very common at all. It was the little things like that were I noticed a trend beginning: Foyt did absolutely no research on African-Americans or any other race for that matter. It is very evident by her constant reliance on black stereotypes applied even to white characters.<br><br><strong>*Warning: Many quote-inducing headdesking ahead.</strong><br><br>Applying black stereotypes to a white female to generate sympathy for the main character:<br><blockquote>"White people were lazy good-for-nothings with weak genetics."</blockquote><br>A black woman's figure categorizing her status in society:<br><blockquote>"Voluptuous, with raisin-colored skin, everything about Ashina screamed ruling class."</blockquote><br>*facepalm*:<br><blockquote>"On the main stage a band of Coals performed in whiteface."</blockquote><br>Oh and I can't forget about the constant theme running rampant that black people are out to get the white people. As if black people, that are now in charge, have nothing else better to do with their time than antagonize others. White women everywhere are doing the <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=0yuFy_qjolU&amp;noredirect=1" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">"White Woman's Workout."</a> &gt;_&gt;<br><br>Every black person in the world is out to get white people:<br><blockquote>"She suspected that each and every Coal passerby wanted to hurt her..."</blockquote><br><p>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380385790i/744853.jpg" alt="" width="356" height="274" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</p><br>It's always black people:<br><blockquote>"All of a sudden, she heard two men behind her. Coals, she figured by their careless, drunken laughter."</blockquote><br>Songs about black men raping a white girl:<br><blockquote>Little Pearly whirly,<br>lost inside the mines;<br>tossed from Coal to Coal, in fear, she whines,<br>"I'm sorry, Mother,<br>he said he only wanted to see my white skin shine."</blockquote><br><a href="http://narwhaler.com/they-raping-everyboy-out-here-antoine-dodson-bed-i-Ahvf4R" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379786923i/489204.jpg" alt="they raping everyboy out here Antoine Dodson / Bed Intruder" width="387" height="297" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Even more rape comparisons:<br><blockquote>She felt more violated than if she'd been raped.</blockquote><br>Go on and scream. Let it out.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380385790ra/744854.gif" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And on and on it goes. But then it gets worse when because there doesn't seem to be any indication that slavery or the Civil Rights Movement ever happened. How was she being oppressed? Well as far as I can tell, white people were well-fed, had their own places, had jobs etc. The biggest thing against them was the mating age, having to wear their "coating" (I'm not sure if that was a law or anything) and getting rude remarks from black people. On a few occasions Eden even wishes the world could go back to a time where white people were free to go outside with their white skin without being persecuted. She frequently says that a black person couldn't possibly understand what it was like to be in her shoes. *slow blink*<br><blockquote>"Someday, when you're locked up in a cage, Bramford, maybe you'll understand what it feels like to be an outcast."<br><br>If only Bramford knew what it was like to be an outcast.<br><br>Maybe now he would know how it felt to be judged by your appearance.<br><br>What did Bramford know about disappointment?</blockquote><br>Yeah, that's not offensive at all. Not one bit. #sarcasm<br><br>And then there is the issue of the FFP A.K.A. the Federation of Free People, "a militant organization of Coals that vowed to rid the planet of Pearls." Pause. *deep breaths* How am I supposed to take that? The Federation of <strong>FREE People</strong>? Get me off this planet. I'm just going to leave that alone before I start seeing blood-red. Too late, I just saw red. Excuse me.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380385791i/744855.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Okay, sorry about that. That was a tad awkward.<br><br>I also want to address the titles given to the races.<br><br>White- Pearls<br><br>Asian- Ambers<br><br>Latino- Tiger Eyes<br><br>Black- Coals<br><br>Albino- Cottons<br><br>Are you kidding me? Coals? As in black as coals? Pearls? As in precious pieces of jewelry? Cotton? As in what my ancestors were forced to pick in the fields? Do I even need to explain how offensive that is? And Foyt's response to the backlash of these titles?<br><blockquote>
  <em>"Why are whites called Pearls, while blacks are called Coals? Imagine a gritty, post-apocalyptic world where all that matters is survival. What good will a pearl do you when luxury items have no use? Coal has energy, fire, and real value. It is durable and strong, not easily crushed like a pearl. Pearl is a pejorative term here. Coals are admired. Coals oppress Pearls because they fear that those with light skin will add to a population unable to survive “The Heat,” and drain meager resources."</em>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380385791ra/744856.gif" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>No, no, no, no. NO! You do not give a title that has been used as a racial slur to a people who have been oppressed. You do not do that. And if you think any of that is okay, something is deeply wrong with you. By no stretch of the imagination can "Pearl" be considered a racial slur. Unless, along with common sense, this society has happened to lose every dictionary in existance. In which case, I shall provide the definition.<br><br><strong>pearl1    [purl] </strong><br><strong>noun</strong><br>1. a smooth, rounded bead formed within the shells of certain mollusks and composed of the mineral aragonite or calcite in a matrix, deposited in concentric layers as a protective coating around an irritating foreign <a href="http://dictionary.reference.com/browse/object" rel="nofollow noopener">object</a>: valued as a gem when lustrous and finely colored. Compare <a href="http://dictionary.reference.com/browse/cultured+pearl" rel="nofollow noopener">cultured pearl</a>.<br>2. something resembling this, as various synthetic substances for use in costume jewelry.<br>3. something similar in form, luster, etc., as a dewdrop or a capsule of medicine.<br>4. something <a href="http://dictionary.reference.com/browse/precious" rel="nofollow noopener">precious</a> or choice; the finest example of anything: pearls of wisdom.<br>5. a very pale gray approaching white but commonly with a bluish tinge.<br><br>Yup, that is just the title I would give to a group that is being oppressed. Tell them they're <em>worthless</em> while giving them a name that <strong>literally means <em>precious.</em></strong> Moreover, if "Coal" supposed to be a positive title, highlighting their strengths, then why is "Cotton" considered derogatory? By definition cotton is a very useful resource. It's strong, durable, able to withstand cold and hot temperatures. So what's the deal here?<br><br><blockquote>Only Cottons, the derogatory word for albinos, were lower, and they were extinct.</blockquote><br>I don't think for a second Fyot didn't know what she was doing when she wrote that because in the beginning of the novel she calls "Coal" a racial slur herself.<br><blockquote>Before she knew it, she blurted out an incendiary racial slur. "Gets your hands off of me, you damn Coal!"</blockquote><br>First of all, I'm surprised she was still alive after saying that to someone of the elite class. Surely if Pearls are so worthless and oppressed, there would be severe consequences for an action like that? Second, Foyt is again baking her cake and trying to stuff her face with it too. Which one is it? It's either a positive term or a racial slur. It cannot be both. I'll tell you what I think. I think Foyt was just trying to smooth things over with her choice of words. And failed, I might add, because my bullshit meter is about to explode.<br><br>In the second half of the novel I had no idea what was going on half the time. The scenes were very jumbled with no clear direction of where the plot was headed. World building left way too many holes in the story. Because surely there are more races on Earth that just the ones listed in <em>Revealing Eden.</em> Character interactions were much of the same confusion. But I think that it mostly had to do with the fact that Eden was a fucking idiot. Her stupidity burned. For real.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380385791ra/744857.gif" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>From this day forward I can never say Bella Swan was the worst. Eden is the worst protagonist I have ever read. Not only does she completely miss the point over and over again, regardless of how many times it is spelled out, but she is extremely selfish and all around unlikable. There is a scene in the novel where Eden happens across an anaconda and I felt myself rooting for the snake. Sadly, he didn't win. *weeps*<br><br>One thing that was clear was how Eden suddenly became attracted to Bramford after he became half beast. One minute she is talking about how sexy he is and the next she is calling him names, even after he saves her life several times. (Bold is mine.)<br><blockquote>That <strong>dumb beast</strong> had been gone since yesterday afternoon.<br><br>And why had she thought the dress would please such an <strong>insensitive brute?</strong><br><br>"Is this where you lock up your victims? <strong>You're an animal,</strong> Bramford."<br><br>The <strong>selfish beast</strong> simply dropped the subject and ignored her.</blockquote><br>Also she likes to ride him like an animal:<br><blockquote>She sunk her fingers into his long silky hair, like reins on a horse. As if she controlled the beast. Eden knew it wasn't true, but she enjoyed the illusion just the same.</blockquote><br>What. The. Hell. A black man is turned into an animal and you have your white protagonist daydreaming about riding him like a frickin' pony? I just... can't.<br><br>When I finally finished reading <em>Revealing Eden</em> I had to ask myself what kind of person would think any of this would be remotely okay? Foyt says:<br><blockquote>"So yes, this book is meant to provoke the white community that has never experienced racism or been oppressed because they have been in the majority in this country."</blockquote><br>I take issue with the white community only able to be provoked by featuring a white girl who is oppressed by black people using the very same stereotypes we fight against everyday. So, yes. I taking extreme offense to that. If Foyt is indeed "color blind" as she claims then making readers connect with a black character shouldn't be a problem for her. But instead she chose to "turn racism on its head" and say, "Black folk, I know you guys have dealt with some really rough shit in the past, but what if it happened to white people?" No, just no. The African-American community exists *because* of the oppression. It is <strong>our</strong> history, <strong>our</strong> roots. It is the one thing that must be left alone. You can't just take that away from us and apply it yourselves and make us look like the bad guys in your novel! This is one of the few times where I had to sit back and wonder who could possibly enjoy this book.<br><blockquote>"And if you ask if all these reviewers are white then consider that you have a racist point of view."</blockquote><br>Oh, really? Racist point of view?  Racism isn't dead. It's something that many of us has to face everyday. As a people, it is ingrained in our society that our features are less desirable than that of whites. There are somethings some people will never understand. They have never had to walk in the shoes of another race and therefore they have limited understanding on what it means to be a Person of Color. When you get followed around in a clothing store because of your skin color, when you can't go into the 7-11 with your hoodie on, when a job tells you your natural hair is "unprofessional," when your 4-year-old daughter asks you why her hair doesn't "go down like a princess" as if hers could never be considered as such, when you see celebrities of your race white washed in ad campaigns, when your male relatives are arrested for <em>looking</em> suspicious, when you see your grandparents cry after Obama was elected because they thought they would never live to see the day where a black man held office, when you know there are some parts of the country where you are just not welcome because of your skin color, or when you walk down the aisle of your local book store and all you see on the book covers are white people, with a small section devoted to African-Americans, you realize you are living in a white world. Racist point of view? Wherever would one have gotten that?<br><br>I think this goes without saying: <strong>NO STARS FOR YOU!</strong><br><br><strong>*SARCASM ALERT*</strong><br><br>You didn't think I'd just leave it on that unhappy note did you? Pfft, as if!<br><br>Ay yo, if black people truly ruled da world we damn sure wouldn't be toting 'round some whack name like "Coals." Naw, we'd go for something MUCH more gangsta like, <strong>Chocolate</strong> <em>Thundas</em>. Then we'd go n' elect Snoop Dogg as our president and Dave Chappelle as our VP, ya feel meh? <strong>We'd give women back control of their bodies.</strong> We'd legalize MJ and the national anthem would be "<a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Wa5B22KAkEk" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Young, Wild and Free</a>."  We'd move the capital to the ATL, where we like to "<a href="http://www.urbandictionary.com/define.php?term=throw%20dem%20bones" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">throw dem bones</a>." <a href="http://www.royalevidds.com/images/grills.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Grillz</a> would be covered by dental insurance. <strong>Free health care to all citizens.</strong> Oppress white people? Naw, we ain't got time fo' dat shit, man! We'd be too busy <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Fg6J1Skptbs" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">spending our reparation money</a> from da Gov'ment, giving back to the economy.<br><br>Chicken spots n' drive through liquor stores would be on every corner. You welcome!  (So what, we get drunk...). 12pm would be a mandatory nation wide nap time, which no one would pay any attention to. Fuck the system! (So what, we don't sleep...). Though dey should 'cause "<a href="http://www.urbandictionary.com/define.php?term=the+itis" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">The Itis</a>" is a very serious condition affecting 1 out of 2 black folk e'rywhere. And finally, random flash mob dances would be to songs like "<a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=zp8wJSndyd4" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Lean Wit It, Rock Wit It</a>" and "<a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=zGt-Wcyhg3o" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">We Fly High</a>" (We just havin' fun and we don't care who sees...).<br><br> <br><p>We stay fly. No lie. You know dis...</p><br><a href="http://cuddlebuggery.com/?attachment_id=12285" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380385791i/744858.png" alt="" width="494" height="356" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>Book was provided by publisher/author via NetGalley for an honest review.</i><br><br>More reviews and other fantastical things at <a href="http://cuddlebuggery.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Cuddlebuggery Book Blog</a>.</span>

<div id="review_378705108" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/378705108" />
    <a title="John Egbert" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5223517-john-egbert"><img alt="John Egbert" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1340483284p2/5223517.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/378705108?book_show_action=true">Jul 28, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="John Egbert" class="user" itemprop="url" name="John Egbert" href="/user/show/5223517-john-egbert">John Egbert</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer378705108" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2201990416878203136">Edit 8/4/2012:<br/><br/>"Conceivably, if the book had not reached the African-American community of readers, if such a category still exists, perhaps there might be some backlash."<br/>-Victoria Foyt<br/><br/>She did not just go there.<br/><br/><i>she did not just go there</i><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/490310.gif' width='400' height='300' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>-<i>some guy on Victoria Foyt</i> (no not really) (but still)<br/><br/>When I get depressed, I don't want to be around other people. I usually sit in an empty room. Sometimes I'll use art therapy and draw something glittery and happy to make me feel better. Other people? They like </span>
  <span id="freeText2201990416878203136" style="display:none">Edit 8/4/2012:<br><br>"Conceivably, if the book had not reached the African-American community of readers, if such a category still exists, perhaps there might be some backlash."<br>-Victoria Foyt<br><br>She did not just go there.<br><br><i>she did not just go there</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/490310.gif" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>-<i>some guy on Victoria Foyt</i> (no not really) (but still)<br><br>When I get depressed, I don't want to be around other people. I usually sit in an empty room. Sometimes I'll use art therapy and draw something glittery and happy to make me feel better. Other people? They like hugs. Me, I hate even being <i>near</i> people when I'm feeling down.<br><br>So now you understand why I spent a lot of time alone after reading the first ten pages of Save the Pearls.<br><br>Art therapy? This is what I drew while fuming and angsting over Save the Pearls:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380385596i/744597._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>I was not a happy camper. There are a multitude of reasons why.<br><br>I mean, even if I were to overlook the blatantly racist premise and plotline, Revealing Eden still sucks.<br><br>The author can't write her way out of a fucking box. First of all, Eden is hardly a <i>character</i>. I've seen potted plants with more personality. I would have rather the book be written from the perspective of a potted plant, in all honesty.<br><br>Revealing Cedar... Save the Trees #1. Would have been more interesting and thought provoking than this.<br><br>But I'm getting away from point. Secondly, if Eden had a personality you would be sure Foyt would tell you exactly what it is. Because she makes sure to tell every fucking other thing. Does this woman even know the meaning of the word "show"?!<br><br>She couldn't have been less subtle if she taped her book to a club and proceeded to whack me over the head.<br><br>The world in which she tries to place us in is so obviously fake. It doesn't feel sci-fi or post apocalyptic. While with good post-apocalyptic books (Angelfall, for instance) I was able to get into the setting almost immediately, every mention of the <i>oh so horrible</i> society Eden was living in had me groaning in agony and clawing at my eyes and face.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380385596ra/744598.gif" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>"Pearls, which was the derogatory term for whites..."<br><br>OH YEAH I'M SURE<br><br>IT CERTAINLY SOUNDS LIKE ONE<br><br>I mentioned in an update how slurs have reasons as to <i>why</i> they are slurs.<br><br>The most infamous n word, as I mentioned, could be translated to mean "black object". So, yeah, you can take a wild guess as to why it's offensive. (For the purpose of now we're going to disregard the hundreds of years of baggage piled on top of that, which is another reason why pearls is shit and doesn't work.)<br><br>A pearl is a precious gem! <i>HOW IS THAT OFFENSIVE?</i> And, okay, even disregarding the fact that it is <i>a precious gem</i> I could say "well maybe they're calling them useless clam spit". But even then, to call another group you're trying to oppress a pearl and <i>then</i> turn around and call yourself a <i>coal</i>? What the motherfuckery...<br><br>I guess the Coals are just that shitty at oppressing people.<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380385596ra/744599.gif" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>The more of the book I read, the more I felt like asking Foyt what the frex <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[yes, I didn't like Across the Universe, but it was 192041412914890125970328190184032539603168+ times better than this fucking shit <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> she was thinking when she wrote this. And I only got to page ten, mind you. <br><br>And even then, at the time I was speechless. Other than the underlying instinctive reaction to deliver a good kick to the crotch of whoever was responsible for this, I think looked pretty much like,<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380385596ra/744600.gif" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Because, how, how can you write this.<br><br>And not know.<br><br>How offensive it is.<br><br>Maybe if Foyt was a teenager, a twelve year old at that, I would have understood. Like how five year olds do the supposedly native american mouth call thing without knowing it's racist because nobody ever told them? Maybe? But Foyt is a grown woman. She should know better. And that only made it <i>worse.</i><br><br>Of course, then there's the obvious. That she does know. And she just doesn't care. Which is what I'm going to assume. <br><br>So, in conclusion, Foyt:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380385596ra/744601.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>DISHONOR ON YOU.<br><br>DISHONOR.<br><br>Because, you know what? You are dishonorable. You are dishonorable for writing this book. You are dishonorable for thinking you're doing anyone a favor by publishing this. <i>You are dishonorable</i>. You have no honor. None. You say you're 'turning the tables on racism'. Oh please. The only thing you're doing is <i>contributing</i> to racism. Yes. It's true. Believe it or not the premise of "white people being oppressed by evil and savage black people" isn't a new thing. You are not original. You are not helping by perpetrating this. You are not helping. <i>Stop.</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379773019i/313942.jpg" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>If you really want to help, you know what you can do?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380385596ra/744602.gif" width="200" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Yes, that is about the only thing <i>you</i> can do to help. Sit in the fucking shame cube and show your remorse for this disgusting "book". Go on, now.<br><br>Everyone who isn't Foyt... I would recommend staying away from this so called novel. Sure, I know that you may be curious, but believe me, it won't cause you anything but pain. And if you're <i>really</i> lucky, it will make you hate humans and feel like shit after you read it. <br><br>Like me.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380385596ra/744603.gif" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Now if you'll excuse me I'm going to consume so much chocolate my very <i>being</i> will become a mix of cacao, sugar and milk. Have a nice day.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_378293917" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/378293917" />
    <a title="Amanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8832724-amanda"><img alt="Amanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1334638535p2/8832724.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/378293917?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda" href="/user/show/8832724-amanda">Amanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">NO ONE</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8832724-amanda?shelf=tried-to-read-but-could-not">tried-to-read-but-could-not</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer378293917" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9717109973500726970">This is a racist piece of shit excuse for a book. I'm sorry, but I can't take a book that "turns the tables on racism" by--once again--victimizing poor, young, fragile caucasian girls and vilifying POC seriously. There is no excuse for blatant racism. The cover of this book uses blackface. One of the core concepts of this book is using blackface.<br/><br/>Pretty blond-haired blue-eyed white girls using blackface is NOT turning the tables on racism. Stop pretending like it is, and stop adding fuel to the f</span>
  <span id="freeText9717109973500726970" style="display:none">This is a racist piece of shit excuse for a book. I'm sorry, but I can't take a book that "turns the tables on racism" by--once again--victimizing poor, young, fragile caucasian girls and vilifying POC seriously. There is no excuse for blatant racism. The cover of this book uses blackface. One of the core concepts of this book is using blackface.<br /><br />Pretty blond-haired blue-eyed white girls using blackface is NOT turning the tables on racism. Stop pretending like it is, and stop adding fuel to the fire.<br /><br />The terms for POC are offensive and ill-issued. Black individuals are referred to as Coals (the image draws to mind dirty, undesirable, disposable); Asian individuals are referred to as Ambers; Latino and Hispanic individuals are referred to as Tiger's-Eyes; meanwhile, caucasians are referred to as Pearls (precious, rare, etc.). THIS IS RACISM. It's not even masked racism; it's in your face, on the page. On page nine, it shines through clear as day--our protagonist refers to a POC as "them." (Italicized, by the way.) <br /><br />Take me back to the time when teenagers read books of solid merit and upstanding moral meaning; perhaps this is the time when dystopian actually meant something in the literary world, where Bradbury and Orwell and Huxley and Atwood and Heinlein and their contemporaries reigned. I'm getting quite tired with the authors who have the strongest influence over today's youth exacerbating a problem rather than attempting to navigate the terrain constructively and without a whiny, self-pitying protagonist floundering in the way.<br /><br />I am ashamed that this book is being taken seriously. I am ashamed that it's winning awards. I am ashamed that people not that much younger than me are the target market and are being exposed to this bullshit. I'm ashamed that a grown-ass woman would think that it's okay for her to write about something that she's never had any kind of experience with. I shouldn't feel the need to apologize for every white writer out there, and it shouldn't be my job. Get this shit off the market and don't let your kids read it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9717109973500726970" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Tenth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11015138-tenth"><img alt="Tenth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353847359p2/11015138.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/378369046?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tenth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tenth" href="/user/show/11015138-tenth">Tenth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11015138-tenth?shelf=racist">racist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11015138-tenth?shelf=didn-t-finish">didn-t-finish</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer378369046" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8818111113735996654">I only read the first chapter of this book, and I barely even made it that far, because this book is so painfully racist.<br/><br/>Supposedly by making white people an oppressed group and black people the dominant group this book 'turns the tables on racism' with the intent of showing readers that racism is bad. But in practise it seems to just be an excuse to frame black people and dangerous and threatening and white people as poor little victims, reenforcing racist stereotypes. Even the title of the ser</span>
  <span id="freeText8818111113735996654" style="display:none">I only read the first chapter of this book, and I barely even made it that far, because this book is so painfully racist.<br /><br />Supposedly by making white people an oppressed group and black people the dominant group this book 'turns the tables on racism' with the intent of showing readers that racism is bad. But in practise it seems to just be an excuse to frame black people and dangerous and threatening and white people as poor little victims, reenforcing racist stereotypes. Even the title of the series "Save the Pearls" (which translates from this book's jargon to "Save the Whites") sounds like the type of thing you come across on racist extremist websites that fearmonger about white people 'dying out' because other races are apparently such a threat. Not to mention that in the society Foyt dreams up white people apparently spend all their time in blackface, a device she uses without seeming to display any sort of knowledge of, or concern about, how it has been historically (and contemporarily, sadly) used as a tool to mock and spread stereotypes about black people.<br /><br />If you want to read YA fiction which genuinely uses the tool of switching around who is the oppressor and oppressed in order to give the reader a different perspective on racism, try Noughts and Crosses by Malorie Blackman. A much less offensive, much more nuanced, and all around better written YA book that explores issues of race.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8818111113735996654" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_378427304" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/378427304" />
    <a title="Isa Lavinia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1016831-isa-lavinia"><img alt="Isa Lavinia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1518528816p2/1016831.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/378427304?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Isa Lavinia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Isa Lavinia" href="/user/show/1016831-isa-lavinia">Isa Lavinia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/13101481-revealing-eden">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">racists, people who are blind to their privilege </span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1016831-isa-lavinia?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1016831-isa-lavinia?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1016831-isa-lavinia?shelf=awful">awful</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1016831-isa-lavinia?shelf=racist">racist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1016831-isa-lavinia?shelf=problematic">problematic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1016831-isa-lavinia?shelf=just-no">just-no</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1016831-isa-lavinia?shelf=bad-science">bad-science</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1016831-isa-lavinia?shelf=tstl">tstl</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1016831-isa-lavinia?shelf=ugh-a-love-triangle">ugh-a-love-triangle</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer378427304" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2013656233261436345">Originally posted at <a href='http://paperbackwonderland.blogspot.pt/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Paperback Wonderland</a>.<br/><br/>This book was one of the most racist things I have ever read.<br/>The bare bones of the plot: a world where black people are the oppressing majority and white people are the oppressed minority. Obviously, the concept isn't new. It was done - and well done, at that - by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/172977.Malorie_Blackman' title='Malorie Blackman' rel='nofollow noopener'>Malorie Blackman</a> in her Noughts and Crosses series. If you're interested in the premise, but you dislike blatant racist propaganda, give that one a try.<br/><br/>You could assume this reversal would serv</span>
  <span id="freeText2013656233261436345" style="display:none">Originally posted at <a href="http://paperbackwonderland.blogspot.pt/" rel="nofollow noopener">Paperback Wonderland</a>.<br><br>This book was one of the most racist things I have ever read.<br>The bare bones of the plot: a world where black people are the oppressing majority and white people are the oppressed minority. Obviously, the concept isn't new. It was done - and well done, at that - by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/172977.Malorie_Blackman" title="Malorie Blackman" rel="nofollow noopener">Malorie Blackman</a> in her Noughts and Crosses series. If you're interested in the premise, but you dislike blatant racist propaganda, give that one a try.<br><br>You could assume this reversal would serve to de-construct issues surrounding racism (as happened in Blackman's books). You'd be wrong. The way this goes about reads more like, "how can we make everyone care about the racism POC have to endure? I know! Let's get a pretty, blond, white girl to go through that!" It's a mockery, a dystopian what-if, with all its horrors, of what is a reality to POC to this very day.<br><br>Foyt doesn't just reverse social roles, as Blackman did, she comes up with a dystopian, post-apocalyptic future in which solar radiation ("The Great Meltdown") killed almost everyone - except most black people.<br>Even though UV radiation's effects on the immune system and eyes are independent of race, and it's never clearly explained how humanity managed to survive in a world where flora and fauna have been decimated - the ever present holograms, as far as I know, won't fill your belly or keep you from getting rickets. But moving on.<br><br>This book is so messed up that I honestly need to give examples so people don't accuse me of making it up. So...<br><br>"<i>Had Peach forgotten that Eden’s skin only had a dark coating? Maybe she was passing, after all. Wouldn’t that be nice?</i>"<br><br>The book starts off with black face and I'm not even going to touch that one, because it's too obvious to anyone with a functional brain. In this book, the author goes so far as to have "<i>a band of Coals</i>" known as "<i>The Lost Caucasians</i>" performing in <b>whiteface</b>. I'm also not going to go off on how problematic the whole issue of passing is. Anyone with the bare minimum knowledge of history already knows it. The author addresses it only as problematic insofar as it is just another way the protagonist fails to see how beautiful she really is. I mean... I mean, really. I don't even know anymore.<br><br>"<i>She was a lowly Pearl, worth nothing in a world ruled by dark-skinned Coals.</i>"<br><br>I'm sure that, if asked, Foyt would have a very witty justification for "Coals" - the way she chose to term the black majority in the book. Exposure to solar radiation will make you perish of "The Heat", and those who survive it are the "Coals" - hahaha, get it?<br>Too bad that when in context - in this case, comparing it to what other races are called - "Coals" is still insulting. Get this, the extinct albinos are "Cottons" (I swear I'm not making this up to better showcase how absurdly racist this is, Foyt really seems to have gone out of her way to be insulting), white people are "Pearls" - of course there are black pearls but let's ignore that and focus on the fact that pearls are precious gems and coals are... coals. So what happened is that, in a dystopia where black people are the ruling class, they chose a derogatory term for themselves? Am I getting this right? Because don't let yourself be fooled, the ruling majority is the one who decides who is who and what is what. So black people decided they would be Coals and white people would be Pearls? Was it a racist naming decision by the author or was it a racist implication that black people are so ignorant they don't even understand the value dissonance of their choice? It's really a choose your flavour of racism issue here.<br><br>Don't let this whole naming thing distract you, even though Pearls are the lowest of the low, the protagonist still finds time in her busy schedule of being oppressed to be racist:<br>"<i>Ashina jumped up and grabbed Eden’s lab coat. “Are you calling me a liar?”<br>Eden flinched. One of them was touching her. White-hot light exploded in her head. Before she knew it, she blurted out an incendiary racial slur.<br>“Get your hands off of me, you damn Coal!”</i>"<br>Can you imagine how this would work out in the real world - I don't even need to add, "back when...", I mean <b>now</b>.<br><br>"<i>Because of </i>[Eden's father]<i> high intelligence scores, they had overlooked his race and given him the position of lead scientist at Resources for Environmental Adaptation, or REA. He even had secured Eden a plum researcher’s job at the lab. They were the only Pearls allowed to work there.</i>"<br><br>Never mind that brilliant POC find their paths barred when they try to make it in Academia today, not even worth mentioning how POC scientists were treated in the real world social period corresponding to this novel. The fact that her father is a "Pearl" but still the lead scientist is, by itself, unbelievable, not only that but he managed to get his 17 year old daughter a position in a top scientific facility. But let us set aside the absurd to explore the ever popular "white man saves the day" aspect of it, shall we? I mean, really, even in a world where they are at the bottom of the social ladder, and all but extinct, the white protagonists still manage to save the "ignorant" POC. Well done. And it gets worse:<br><br>"<i>Eden might be powerless, but she smiled at the secret knowledge that she was one of only three people who understood how he was about to change the world, and possibly, even save it.</i>"<br>Not only do white people save the day, but the POC don't just lack the ability to save themselves, they lack the very capacity to even understand how it happens at all.<br><br>"<i>If Eden wasn't mated in six months when she turned eighteen—the deadline for girls—she'd be cut off from Basic Resources, and left outside to die.</i>"<br><br>Why? Why provide this incentive for the reproduction of a race deemed inferior? Let's take a look at how that worked out in the real world. African slaves who their owners thought were no better than animals, were bred as such, to make strong slaves, thus serving a purpose to their exploiting oppressors. However, in this world, "Pearls" don't seem to fare too well. Their position would be even less regarded than Native populations back in the day, I mean, at least the Natives didn't just up and die if left on their own as Pearls do - and what happened to Natives under the colonizers? Genocide, that's what. They scattered them, took away their lands and resources, took the children away from their parents to effectively destroy their culture and, to this day they are extremely oppressed. There are no incentives given to rebuild their great nations, be it in the US, be it in Canada, be it in Australia, Native populations are always amongst the poorest.<br>But I guess the "Pearls" would have to "get mated" because how can you have a YA book without the heroine discovering that her reason to go on is finding and keeping a man? Unthinkable.<br><br>Bramford, her boss and potential romantic interest has skin "<i>the color of storm clouds</i>" so I don't know if Foyt was being poetic and saying he was dark, or being insulting and saying he was ashy to the nth degree, like, "That dude really needs some lotion, his skin... storms a brewing. You see that man and he only makes sense in a production of The Tempest, hovering overhead".<br><br>Jamal (of course, he'd be named Jamal, of course) "<i>My Dark Prince</i>" (Eden's words, not mine), her other love interest "<i>Unlike most of his kind, he was colorblind</i>" - I don't know how, in this day and age, an author - therefore a person who knows how to read - has not yet grasped the concept that being "colorblind" regarding race is, in fact, racist. You have to be in a position of privilege to have the option to ignore race, if you check your privilege you will not say ignorant things like, "I don't see race." Really, it's not a complicated concept.<br><br>Eden, as a character, is horrible. Whiny, racist, full of self hatred and always expecting her problems will be solved by her "Dark Prince" who always calls her "Little Bunny" and "pet" and despite this she can't wait to be mated to him and have his babies. I thought it unlikely he'd be interested in her, considering her personality alone all issues of race aside <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[and of course he was only using her, but it's hard to feel bad for her because she was only using him as well. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>And if all this mess wasn't bad enough there was some bestiality sprinkled on top of the whole thing.<br><br>By the way, I think Foyt forgot something in her list of "thank yous":<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380385554i/744524.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="2013656233261436345" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
